## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The governing equation generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and/or parametric/external driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (Duffing with periodic drive)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (van der Pol-type damping term)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * x**3 (parametric + nonlinear restoring)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * v (combined Duffing and van der Pol)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring force ŌåÆ only odd powers of x (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) indicating symmetric potential well
- Asymmetric potential ŌåÆ even powers of x (x┬▓) present in restoring force, indicating broken symmetry
- Self-sustained oscillations ŌåÆ damping coefficient changes sign with amplitude, e.g., v*(1 - x┬▓) or v*(c0 + c1*x┬▓)
- Parametric excitation ŌåÆ position term multiplied by periodic function of time, e.g., x*cos(c*t)
- Energy-dependent frequency ŌåÆ cubic term x┬│ causes amplitude-dependent oscillation frequency (Duffing hallmark)
- Nonlinear dissipation ŌåÆ velocity terms coupled with position powers (v*x┬▓, v*xŌü┤) indicate amplitude-dependent energy loss
- Hardening vs softening spring ŌåÆ sign of cubic coefficient: positive x┬│ = hardening, negative x┬│ = softening
- Limit cycle behavior ŌåÆ competing linear negative damping and nonlinear positive damping terms (c0*v + c1*v*x┬▓ with opposite signs)
